**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

- `github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/kafka--0753c489$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc$` filter
- `github.com/sg-evals/camel--1006f047` — use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/camel--1006f047$` filter

Scope ALL keyword_search/nls_search queries to these repos.
Use the repo name as the `repo` parameter for read_file/go_to_definition/find_references.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Flink DataStream API Deprecation Markers

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/flink under flink-streaming-java/src/ that contain @Deprecated annotations on DataStream API classes or methods. For each deprecated class, identify the class name and the recommended replacement (noted in the deprecation javadoc). Focus on deprecated source functions, sink functions, timestamp extractors, and I/O format classes.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the migration domain.

Perfect! I've successfully identified all the deprecated DataStream API classes in the Apache Flink repository under `flink-streaming-java/src/`. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Deprecated DataStream API Classes Found:

1. **AscendingTimestampExtractor** - Timestamp extractor for monotonously ascending timestamps → Replace with `TimestampAssigner` and `WatermarkStrategies`

2. **DataGeneratorSource** - Source function for data generation → Replace with `org.apache.flink.connector.datagen.source.DataGeneratorSource`

3. **DiscardingSink** - Sink that ignores elements → Replace with `org.apache.flink.streaming.api.functions.sink.v2.DiscardingSink`

4. **StreamingFileSink** - Sink for writing to filesystem files → Replace with `org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink`

5. **TextInputFormat** - Input format for text files → Replace with `FLIP-27 FileSource` and `Sink-V2 FlinkSink`

6. **TextOutputFormat** - Output format for text files → Replace with `FLIP-27 FileSource` and `Sink-V2 FlinkSink`

7. **TwoPhaseCommitSinkFunction** - Base class for exactly-once sinks → Replace with `org.apache.flink.api.connector.sink2.Sink`

The answer has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete file paths, symbol names, and detailed information about each deprecated class and its recommended replacement.

The reason for this is how the sink works together with the checkpointing mechanism to\n87:  * provide exactly-once semantics and fault-tolerance. The part file that is currently being written\n88:  * to is {@code in-progress}. Once a part file is closed for writing it becomes {@code pending}.\n89:  * When a checkpoint is successful the currently pending files will be moved to {@code finished}.\n90:  *\n91:  * <p>If case of a failure, and in order to guarantee exactly-once semantics, the sink should roll\n92:  * back to the state it had when that last successful checkpoint occurred. To this end, when\n93:  * restoring, the restored files in {@code pending} state are transferred into the {@code finished}\n94:  * state while any {@code in-progress} files are rolled back, so that they do not contain data that\n95:  * arrived after the checkpoint from which we restore.\n96:  *\n97:  * @param <IN> Type of the elements emitted by this sink\n98:  * @deprecated Use {@link org.apache.flink.connector.file.sink.FileSink} instead.\n99:  */\n100: @Internal\n101: public class StreamingFileSink<IN> extends RichSinkFunction<IN>\n102:         implements CheckpointedFunction, CheckpointListener {\n103: \n104:     private static final long serialVersionUID = 1L;\n105: \n106:     // ------------------------ configuration fields --------------------------\n107: \n108:     private final long bucketCheckInterval;\n109: \n110:     private final BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ? extends BucketsBuilder<IN, ?, ?>> bucketsBuilder;\n111: \n112:     // --------------------------- runtime fields -----------------------------\n113: \n114:     private transient StreamingFileSinkHelper<IN> helper;\n115: \n116:     /**\n117:      * Creates a new {@code StreamingFileSink} that writes files to the given base directory with\n118:      * the give buckets properties.\n119:      */\n120:     @VisibleForTesting\n121: ",
